**Tool Call: Read file `README.md`**
Status: Completed

````bird-denoising-new/README.md
# ViTVS Audio Denoising

This repository contains the PyTorch Lightning implementation of Vision Transformer Segmentation (ViTVS) specifically designed for Audio Denoising (e.g., separating bird sounds from noise). 

It converts audio into spectrograms, passes them through a ViT Encoder-Decoder architecture to generate a Binary Mask, and reconstructs the clean audio using ISTFT.

## Project Structure

- `config.py`: Hyperparameters and dataset paths.
- `dataset.py`: PyTorch `Dataset` for converting `.wav` to spectrograms and computing the Ideal Binary Mask.
- `model.py`: PyTorch implementation of the ViTVS Encoder and Decoder.
- `lightning_module.py`: PyTorch Lightning wrapper for training and optimization.
- `train.py`: CLI script to train the model with automatic resume capability.
- `test.py`: CLI script to denoise a single audio file using a trained checkpoint.

## Setup

1. Install requirements:
   ```bash
   pip install -r requirements.txt
   ```

2. Prepare your dataset:
   Place your audio files in the `data/` folder (or specify custom paths in `config.py`):
   - `data/train/noisy/*.wav` and `data/train/clean/*.wav`
   - `data/valid/noisy/*.wav` and `data/valid/clean/*.wav`
   - `data/test/noisy/*.wav` and `data/test/clean/*.wav`

## Training

Run the training script. It will automatically save checkpoints to the `checkpoints/` folder. If training is interrupted, simply run the command again and it will resume from the last saved `.ckpt`.

```bash
python train.py
```

You can also override hyperparameters via CLI:
```bash
python train.py --epochs 100 --batch_size 8 --lr 0.0001
```

## Inference / Testing

To denoise an audio file using a trained checkpoint:

```bash
python test.py --ckpt checkpoints/vitvs_denoising/last.ckpt --input test_noisy.wav --output test_clean.wav
```

````


**Tool Call: Read file `src/model.py`**
Status: Completed

```bird-denoising-new/src/model.py
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from einops import rearrange
from einops.layers.torch import Rearrange

class FeedForward(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, dim, hidden_dim, dropout=0.):
        super().__init__()
        self.net = nn.Sequential(
            nn.LayerNorm(dim),
            nn.Linear(dim, hidden_dim),
            nn.GELU(),
            nn.Dropout(dropout),
            nn.Linear(hidden_dim, dim),
            nn.Dropout(dropout)
        )
    def forward(self, x):
        return self.net(x)

class Attention(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, dim, heads=8, dim_head=64, dropout=0.):
        super().__init__()
        inner_dim = dim_head * heads
        self.heads = heads
        self.scale = dim_head ** -0.5
        self.norm = nn.LayerNorm(dim)

        self.attend = nn.Softmax(dim=-1)
        self.dropout = nn.Dropout(dropout)
        self.to_qkv = nn.Linear(dim, inner_dim * 3, bias=False)
        self.to_out = nn.Sequential(nn.Linear(inner_dim, dim), nn.Dropout(dropout))

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.norm(x)
        qkv = self.to_qkv(x).chunk(3, dim=-1)
        q, k, v = map(lambda t: rearrange(t, 'b n (h d) -> b h n d', h=self.heads), qkv)

        dots = torch.matmul(q, k.transpose(-1, -2)) * self.scale
        attn = self.attend(dots)
        attn = self.dropout(attn)

        out = torch.matmul(attn, v)
        out = rearrange(out, 'b h n d -> b n (h d)')
        return self.to_out(out)

class Transformer(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, dim, depth, heads, dim_head, mlp_dim, dropout=0.):
        super().__init__()
        self.layers = nn.ModuleList([])
        for _ in range(depth):
            self.layers.append(nn.ModuleList([
                Attention(dim, heads=heads, dim_head=dim_head, dropout=dropout),
                FeedForward(dim, mlp_dim, dropout=dropout)
            ]))
    def forward(self, x):
        for attn, ff in self.layers:
            x = attn(x) + x
            x = ff(x) + x
        return x

class ViTVS_Encoder(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, image_size, patch_size, dim, depth, heads, mlp_dim, channels=1):
        super().__init__()
        num_patches = (image_size // patch_size) ** 2
        patch_dim = channels * patch_size ** 2

        self.to_patch_embedding = nn.Sequential(
            Rearrange('b c (h p1) (w p2) -> b (h w) (p1 p2 c)', p1=patch_size, p2=patch_size),
            nn.Linear(patch_dim, dim),
        )
        self.pos_embedding = nn.Parameter(torch.randn(1, num_patches, dim))
        self.transformer = Transformer(dim, depth, heads, dim_head=dim//heads, mlp_dim=mlp_dim)

    def forward(self, img):
        x = self.to_patch_embedding(img)
        b, n, _ = x.shape
        x += self.pos_embedding[:, :n]
        return self.transformer(x)

class ViTVS_Decoder(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, image_size, patch_size, dim, depth, heads, mlp_dim, channels=1):
        super().__init__()
        self.image_size = image_size
        self.patch_size = patch_size
        patch_dim = channels * patch_size ** 2

        self.transformer = Transformer(dim, depth, heads, dim_head=dim//heads, mlp_dim=mlp_dim)

        self.decoder_projection = nn.Sequential(
            nn.Linear(dim, patch_dim),
            nn.LayerNorm(patch_dim)
        )
        self.to_pixels = nn.Linear(patch_dim, patch_size * patch_size)

    def forward(self, x):
        x = self.transformer(x)
        x = self.decoder_projection(x)
        x = self.to_pixels(x)
        # Unfold 1D back to 2D Image
        h = w = self.image_size // self.patch_size
        x = rearrange(x, 'b (h w) (p1 p2) -> b 1 (h p1) (w p2)', h=h, w=w, p1=self.patch_size, p2=self.patch_size)
        return x

class ViTVS(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, config):
        super().__init__()
        self.encoder = ViTVS_Encoder(
            image_size=config.IMAGE_SIZE, patch_size=config.PATCH_SIZE, 
            dim=config.DIM, depth=config.DEPTH, heads=config.HEADS, mlp_dim=config.MLP_DIM
        )
        self.decoder = ViTVS_Decoder(
            image_size=config.IMAGE_SIZE, patch_size=config.PATCH_SIZE, 
            dim=config.DIM, depth=config.DEPTH, heads=config.HEADS, mlp_dim=config.MLP_DIM
        )

    def forward(self, img):
        encoded = self.encoder(img)
        decoded = self.decoder(encoded)
        # Sigmoid for binary mask probabilities [0, 1]
        return torch.sigmoid(decoded)

```


**Tool Call: Read file `src/dataset.py`**
Status: Completed

```bird-denoising-new/src/dataset.py
import os
import glob
import librosa
import numpy as np
import torch
import torchaudio
from torch.utils.data import Dataset, DataLoader

class BirdAudioDataset(Dataset):
    def __init__(self, noisy_dir, clean_dir, config):
        self.noisy_files = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(noisy_dir, '*.wav')))
        self.clean_files = sorted(glob.glob(os.path.join(clean_dir, '*.wav')))
        self.config = config
        
        if len(self.noisy_files) == 0:
            print(f"Warning: No .wav files found in {noisy_dir}")
        elif len(self.noisy_files) != len(self.clean_files):
            print("Warning: Number of noisy and clean files do not match!")

    def __len__(self):
        return len(self.noisy_files)

    def _pad_or_crop_spectrogram(self, spec):
        target_size = self.config.IMAGE_SIZE
        h, w = spec.shape
        
        # Pad or crop height (frequency)
        if h < target_size:
            spec = np.pad(spec, ((0, target_size - h), (0, 0)), mode='constant')
        else:
            spec = spec[:target_size, :]
            
        # Pad or crop width (time)
        if w < target_size:
            spec = np.pad(spec, ((0, 0), (0, target_size - w)), mode='constant')
        else:
            spec = spec[:, :target_size]
            
        return spec

    def _robust_load(self, path):
        try:
            waveform, sr = torchaudio.load(path)
            if waveform.shape[0] > 1:
                waveform = torch.mean(waveform, dim=0, keepdim=True)
            if sr != self.config.SR:
                waveform = torchaudio.functional.resample(waveform, sr, self.config.SR)
            return waveform.squeeze(0).numpy()
        except Exception as e:
            return None

    def __getitem__(self, idx):
        noisy_path = self.noisy_files[idx]
        clean_path = self.clean_files[idx]
        
        # Load audio safely
        noisy_audio = self._robust_load(noisy_path)
        clean_audio = self._robust_load(clean_path)
        
        if noisy_audio is None or clean_audio is None:
            return torch.zeros(1, self.config.IMAGE_SIZE, self.config.IMAGE_SIZE), torch.zeros(1, self.config.IMAGE_SIZE, self.config.IMAGE_SIZE)
            

        # STFT
        noisy_stft = librosa.stft(noisy_audio, n_fft=self.config.N_FFT, 
                                  hop_length=self.config.HOP_LENGTH, win_length=self.config.WIN_LENGTH)
        clean_stft = librosa.stft(clean_audio, n_fft=self.config.N_FFT, 
                                  hop_length=self.config.HOP_LENGTH, win_length=self.config.WIN_LENGTH)
        
        noisy_mag = np.abs(noisy_stft)
        clean_mag = np.abs(clean_stft)
        
        # Ensure both spectrograms have the same number of frames
        min_frames = min(noisy_mag.shape[1], clean_mag.shape[1])
        noisy_mag = noisy_mag[:, :min_frames]
        clean_mag = clean_mag[:, :min_frames]
        
        # Ideal Binary Mask (IBM): Nilai 1 jika magnitudo suara dominan
        mask = (clean_mag > 0.5 * noisy_mag).astype(np.float32)
        
        # Log-scale Normalize Input
        noisy_mag_db = librosa.amplitude_to_db(noisy_mag, ref=np.max)
        noisy_mag_norm = (noisy_mag_db - noisy_mag_db.min()) / (noisy_mag_db.max() - noisy_mag_db.min() + 1e-8)
        
        # Pad/Crop to target IMAGE_SIZE x IMAGE_SIZE
        noisy_mag_norm = self._pad_or_crop_spectrogram(noisy_mag_norm)
        mask = self._pad_or_crop_spectrogram(mask)
        
        # Add channel dimension
        x = torch.from_numpy(noisy_mag_norm).unsqueeze(0).float()
        y = torch.from_numpy(mask).unsqueeze(0).float()
        
        return x, y

def get_dataloader(noisy_dir, clean_dir, config, shuffle=True):
    dataset = BirdAudioDataset(noisy_dir, clean_dir, config)
    return DataLoader(dataset, batch_size=config.BATCH_SIZE, shuffle=shuffle, num_workers=0)

```


**Tool Call: Read file `src/lightning_module.py`**
Status: Completed

```bird-denoising-new/src/lightning_module.py
import pytorch_lightning as pl
import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from src.model import ViTVS

class ViTVSLightningModule(pl.LightningModule):
    def __init__(self, config):
        super().__init__()
        # Ensure config properties are serializable, avoiding the raw class object
        self.save_hyperparameters(
            {k: v for k, v in config.__dict__.items() if not k.startswith('__')}
        )
        self.config = config
        self.model = ViTVS(config)
        self.criterion = nn.BCELoss() # Binary Cross Entropy for mask prediction

    def forward(self, x):
        return self.model(x)

    def training_step(self, batch, batch_idx):
        x, y = batch
        y_hat = self(x)
        loss = self.criterion(y_hat, y)
        self.log('train_loss', loss, on_step=True, on_epoch=True, prog_bar=True, logger=True)
        return loss

    def validation_step(self, batch, batch_idx):
        x, y = batch
        y_hat = self(x)
        loss = self.criterion(y_hat, y)
        self.log('val_loss', loss, on_epoch=True, prog_bar=True, logger=True)
        return loss

    def configure_optimizers(self):
        optimizer = torch.optim.Adam(self.parameters(), lr=self.config.LR)
        return optimizer

```


**Tool Call: Read file `src/config.py`**

```bird-denoising-new/src/config.py
import os

class Config:
    # Training Parameters
    EPOCHS = 50
    BATCH_SIZE = 4
    LR = 1e-4
    
    # Audio parameters
    SR = 16000
    N_FFT = 512
    HOP_LENGTH = 256
    WIN_LENGTH = 512
    
    # Model parameters (ViT)
    IMAGE_SIZE = 256  # Size of Spectrogram patch (256x256)
    PATCH_SIZE = 16   # Patch size for ViT
    DIM = 512
    DEPTH = 12        # 12 Layers of ViT Blocks
    HEADS = 8
    MLP_DIM = 2048
    
    # Default Paths (Can be overridden via CLI)
    BASE_DIR = os.path.dirname(os.path.dirname(os.path.abspath(__file__)))
    DATASET_PATH = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, 'data')
    NOISY_TRAIN_DIR = os.path.join(DATASET_PATH, 'train', 'noisy')
    CLEAN_TRAIN_DIR = os.path.join(DATASET_PATH, 'train', 'clean')
    NOISY_VALID_DIR = os.path.join(DATASET_PATH, 'valid', 'noisy')
    CLEAN_VALID_DIR = os.path.join(DATASET_PATH, 'valid', 'clean')
    NOISY_TEST_DIR = os.path.join(DATASET_PATH, 'test', 'noisy')
    CLEAN_TEST_DIR = os.path.join(DATASET_PATH, 'test', 'clean')
    CHECKPOINT_DIR = os.path.join(BASE_DIR, 'checkpoints', 'vitvs_denoising')

# Ensure checkpoint dir exists
os.makedirs(Config.CHECKPOINT_DIR, exist_ok=True)

```


**Tool Call: Read file `train.py`**
Status: Completed

```bird-denoising-new/train.py
import os
import glob
import argparse
import pytorch_lightning as pl
from pytorch_lightning.callbacks import ModelCheckpoint
import torch

from src.config import Config
from src.dataset import get_dataloader
from src.lightning_module import ViTVSLightningModule

def get_latest_checkpoint(checkpoint_dir):
    checkpoints = glob.glob(os.path.join(checkpoint_dir, '*.ckpt'))
    if not checkpoints:
        return None
    return max(checkpoints, key=os.path.getctime)

def main(args):
    # Override config with CLI args
    Config.EPOCHS = args.epochs
    Config.BATCH_SIZE = args.batch_size
    Config.LR = args.lr
    
    if args.noisy_dir: Config.NOISY_TRAIN_DIR = args.noisy_dir
    if args.clean_dir: Config.CLEAN_TRAIN_DIR = args.clean_dir
    if args.val_noisy_dir: Config.NOISY_VALID_DIR = args.val_noisy_dir
    if args.val_clean_dir: Config.CLEAN_VALID_DIR = args.val_clean_dir
    if args.checkpoint_dir: Config.CHECKPOINT_DIR = args.checkpoint_dir

    print(f"Preparing train dataset from: {Config.NOISY_TRAIN_DIR} and {Config.CLEAN_TRAIN_DIR}")
    train_loader = get_dataloader(Config.NOISY_TRAIN_DIR, Config.CLEAN_TRAIN_DIR, Config)
    
    print(f"Preparing validation dataset from: {Config.NOISY_VALID_DIR} and {Config.CLEAN_VALID_DIR}")
    val_loader = get_dataloader(Config.NOISY_VALID_DIR, Config.CLEAN_VALID_DIR, Config, shuffle=False)
    
    if len(train_loader.dataset) == 0:
        print("Error: Dataset is empty. Please check your data paths.")
        return

    model = ViTVSLightningModule(Config)

    val_checkpoint = ModelCheckpoint(
        dirpath=Config.CHECKPOINT_DIR,
        filename='vitvs-best-val-epoch{epoch:02d}-val_loss{val_loss:.3f}',
        auto_insert_metric_name=False,
        save_top_k=1,
        monitor='val_loss',
        mode='min',
        save_last=True
    )

    train_checkpoint = ModelCheckpoint(
        dirpath=Config.CHECKPOINT_DIR,
        filename='vitvs-best-train-epoch{epoch:02d}-train_loss{train_loss:.3f}',
        auto_insert_metric_name=False,
        save_top_k=1,
        monitor='train_loss',
        mode='min',
    )

    trainer = pl.Trainer(
        max_epochs=Config.EPOCHS,
        accelerator='gpu' if torch.cuda.is_available() else 'cpu',
        devices=1,
        callbacks=[val_checkpoint, train_checkpoint]
    )

    latest_ckpt = get_latest_checkpoint(Config.CHECKPOINT_DIR)

    if latest_ckpt:
        print(f"\n[INFO] Resuming training from Checkpoint: {latest_ckpt}")
        trainer.fit(model, train_dataloaders=train_loader, val_dataloaders=val_loader, ckpt_path=latest_ckpt)
    else:
        print("\n[INFO] Starting training from scratch (Epoch 0)")
        trainer.fit(model, train_dataloaders=train_loader, val_dataloaders=val_loader)

if __name__ == '__main__':
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description='Train ViTVS Audio Denoising Model')
    parser.add_argument('--epochs', type=int, default=Config.EPOCHS, help='Number of epochs')
    parser.add_argument('--batch_size', type=int, default=Config.BATCH_SIZE, help='Batch size')
    parser.add_argument('--lr', type=float, default=Config.LR, help='Learning rate')
    parser.add_argument('--noisy_dir', type=str, default='', help='Path to noisy train data')
    parser.add_argument('--clean_dir', type=str, default='', help='Path to clean train data')
    parser.add_argument('--val_noisy_dir', type=str, default='', help='Path to noisy validation data')
    parser.add_argument('--val_clean_dir', type=str, default='', help='Path to clean validation data')
    parser.add_argument('--checkpoint_dir', type=str, default='', help='Directory to save checkpoints')
    
    args = parser.parse_args()
    main(args)

```


**Tool Call: Read file `test.py`**
Status: Completed

```bird-denoising-new/test.py
import os
import argparse
import librosa
import numpy as np
import soundfile as sf
import torch

from src.config import Config
from src.lightning_module import ViTVSLightningModule

def test_denoising(checkpoint_path, audio_path, output_path='cleaned_audio.wav'):
    print(f"Loading model weights from {checkpoint_path}...")
    model = ViTVSLightningModule.load_from_checkpoint(checkpoint_path, config=Config)
    model.eval()
    device = 'cuda' if torch.cuda.is_available() else 'cpu'
    model.to(device)

    print(f"Processing audio: {audio_path}")
    audio, sr = librosa.load(audio_path, sr=Config.SR)
    stft = librosa.stft(audio, n_fft=Config.N_FFT, hop_length=Config.HOP_LENGTH, win_length=Config.WIN_LENGTH)
    mag = np.abs(stft)
    phase = np.angle(stft)
    
    # Normalize Magnitude
    mag_db = librosa.amplitude_to_db(mag, ref=np.max)
    mag_norm = (mag_db - mag_db.min()) / (mag_db.max() - mag_db.min() + 1e-8)
    
    target_size = Config.IMAGE_SIZE
    h, w = mag_norm.shape
    
    # Pad frequency axis if necessary
    if h < target_size:
        mag_norm = np.pad(mag_norm, ((0, target_size - h), (0, 0)), mode='constant')
        mag_ori_padded = np.pad(mag, ((0, target_size - h), (0, 0)), mode='constant')
        phase_padded = np.pad(phase, ((0, target_size - h), (0, 0)), mode='constant')
    else:
        mag_norm = mag_norm[:target_size, :]
        mag_ori_padded = mag[:target_size, :]
        phase_padded = phase[:target_size, :]

    reconstructed_mag = np.zeros_like(mag_ori_padded)
    
    # Process chunks over time window
    with torch.no_grad():
        for i in range(0, w, target_size):
            chunk = mag_norm[:, i:i+target_size]
            actual_chunk_w = chunk.shape[1]
            
            if actual_chunk_w < target_size:
                chunk = np.pad(chunk, ((0, 0), (0, target_size - actual_chunk_w)), mode='constant')
                
            x_tensor = torch.from_numpy(chunk).unsqueeze(0).unsqueeze(0).float().to(device)
            
            # Forward pass to get Binary Mask
            predicted_mask = model(x_tensor).squeeze().cpu().numpy()
            valid_mask = predicted_mask[:, :actual_chunk_w]
            
            # Apply Mask (Dot Product)
            reconstructed_mag[:, i:i+actual_chunk_w] = mag_ori_padded[:, i:i+actual_chunk_w] * valid_mask
            
    # Pad back to original frequency bins if it was cropped
    if reconstructed_mag.shape[0] < h:
        pad_size = h - reconstructed_mag.shape[0]
        reconstructed_mag = np.pad(reconstructed_mag, ((0, pad_size), (0, 0)), mode='constant')
    else:
        reconstructed_mag = reconstructed_mag[:h, :]
        
    phase_original = phase[:h, :]
    # ISTFT to reconstruct waveform
    complex_spec = reconstructed_mag * np.exp(1j * phase_original)
    clean_audio = librosa.istft(complex_spec, hop_length=Config.HOP_LENGTH, win_length=Config.WIN_LENGTH)
    
    sf.write(output_path, clean_audio, sr)
    print(f"Success! Denoised audio saved to: {output_path}")

if __name__ == '__main__':
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(description='Test ViTVS Audio Denoising')
    parser.add_argument('--ckpt', type=str, required=True, help='Path to checkpoint (.ckpt file)')
    parser.add_argument('--input', type=str, required=True, help='Path to noisy input .wav file')
    parser.add_argument('--output', type=str, default='cleaned_audio.wav', help='Path to save clean .wav file')
    
    args = parser.parse_args()
    
    if not os.path.exists(args.ckpt):
        print(f"Error: Checkpoint file not found: {args.ckpt}")
    elif not os.path.exists(args.input):
        print(f"Error: Input audio file not found: {args.input}")
    else:
        test_denoising(args.ckpt, args.input, args.output)

```

**Tool Call: Read file `PRD.md`**
Status: Completed

```bird-denoising-new/PRD.md
# Product Requirements Document (PRD): ViTVS Code Reproduction (Notebook)

## 1. Tujuan Utama
Menulis kode dari nol untuk mereproduksi arsitektur **Vision Transformer Segmentation (ViTVS)** khusus untuk *Audio Denoising* (memisahkan suara burung dari noise). Hasil akhir harus berupa satu file `notebook.ipynb` yang siap dijalankan di Google Colab (GPU T4) tanpa error.

## 2. Referensi GitHub & Standar Pustaka (Wajib Dipakai)
Kode harus dirakit dengan mengadopsi pola dari repositori berikut:
1. **`lucidrains/vit-pytorch`**: Gunakan pola kode dari repositori ini untuk membangun blok **Encoder** (Vision Transformer dengan Multi-head Self-Attention).
2. **`qubvel/segmentation_models.pytorch`**: Gunakan pola dari repositori ini untuk mengelola bentuk **Decoder** dan proyeksi *output* menjadi Peta Segmentasi Biner (*Binary Mask*).
3. **`Lightning-AI/pytorch-lightning`**: Gunakan *framework* ini untuk membungkus model (sebagai `LightningModule`). Ini wajib untuk menyederhanakan *training loop* dan otomatisasi *checkpoint*.
4. **`librosa` / `torchaudio`**: Gunakan untuk konversi STFT (Audio ke Spectrogram) dan ISTFT (Spectrogram + Phase ke Audio).

## 3. Spesifikasi Arsitektur Pipeline
- **Input:** File `.wav` -> STFT -> Magnitude Spectrogram -> Normalisasi -> Potong jadi *patches* $p \times p$. (Pastikan *Phase* disimpan terpisah).
- **Model Utama:** - Encoder: 12 lapis ViT blocks.
  - Decoder: 12 lapis blok dengan *unfolding* untuk rekonstruksi gambar.
  - Output: Binary Mask (ukuran sama dengan input spectrogram).
- **Output:** Spectrogram input dikalikan (dot product) dengan Binary Mask -> ISTFT dengan *Phase* asli -> File `.wav` bersih.
- **Loss & Optimizer:** Binary Cross-Entropy (BCE) Loss dan Adam Optimizer.

## 4. Struktur File `notebook.ipynb` (Fokus Pembuatan Kode)
AI harus menghasilkan kode terstruktur untuk cell-cell berikut:

- **Cell 1: Setup & Import**
  - Instalasi Pytorch Lightning, librosa, torchaudio.
  - Automount Google Drive (`/content/drive`).
- **Cell 2: Konfigurasi & Hyperparameters**
  - `EPOCHS = 50`, `BATCH_SIZE = 4`, `LR = 1e-4`.
  - Definisi path dataset dan folder `/checkpoints/` di Google Drive.
- **Cell 3: Custom Dataset (PyTorch)**
  - Class DataLoader yang mengkonversi audio menjadi spectrogram (input) dan memuat mask murni (target).
- **Cell 4: Definisi Arsitektur ViTVS**
  - Implementasi class Pytorch murni untuk `ViTVS_Encoder` dan `ViTVS_Decoder`.
- **Cell 5: PyTorch Lightning Module**
  - Bungkus arsitektur ke dalam `pl.LightningModule`. Tulis fungsi `forward`, `training_step`, dan `configure_optimizers`.
- **Cell 6: Training Orchestration (Anti-Timeout Colab)**
  - Konfigurasi `ModelCheckpoint` untuk menyimpan file `.ckpt` ke GDrive.
  - Logika krusial: Jika file checkpoint sebelumnya ada di GDrive, `Trainer.fit()` harus otomatis melakukan *resume training*.
- **Cell 7: Modul Testing (Epoch 8 Evaluator)**
  - Fungsi `test_denoising(checkpoint_path, audio_path)`.
  - Fungsi untuk memuat bobot dari file `.ckpt` (misal dari Epoch 8), memproses satu file audio, dan menghasilkan file `.wav` hasil *denoising*.
```

# ViTVS (ViT for Audio Denoising) — Deep Comparative Analysis Against Similar Projects

## Executive Summary

Your **ViTVS** project sits at a genuinely interesting crossroads between computer vision and audio signal processing, applying segmentation-style ViT to a bird sound denoising problem. The approach is creative and has real academic precedent, but several design choices diverge meaningfully from both the closest peer projects and the current state-of-the-art. Here's the full breakdown.

---

## 🔍 Landscape of Similar Projects Found

### Category 1: Most Directly Comparable — Bird Sound Denoising with Spectrogram-as-Image

| Project | Method | Language | Venue | Key Difference |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **YoushanZhang/BirdSoundsDenoising** ⭐ *Closest peer* | STFT→image, segmentation CNN (DVAD), few-shot mask labeling, MATLAB pipeline | MATLAB | WACV 2023 | Uses a CNN segmentation model (not ViT); masks are *manually labeled* by human annotators via an "ImageMask tool", not computed from clean/noisy ratio |
| **frbicudo/Entropy-Denoiser** | Entropy-based sliding-window thresholding on spectrogram magnitude | Python | – | Traditional/rule-based; no DL |
| **BirdVox/birdvoxdetect** | PCEN normalization + CNN on mel-spectrograms for *detection* (not denoising) | Python | PLOS ONE 2019 | Detection task, not separation; uses PCEN instead of dB scaling |
| **birdnet-team/BirdBox** | YOLO on spectrogram images for call *detection* | Python | Active dev 2025 | Detection/localization, not denoising |

**Key finding:** `BirdSoundsDenoising` (WACV 2023) is your closest published peer. It frames the problem identically (audio denoising = image segmentation on STFT spectrograms) but uses a CNN and *human-annotated* masks rather than IBM. Your project automates the mask generation via IBM, which is a significant advantage.

---

### Category 2: ViT Applied to Audio Spectrograms

| Project | Method | Stars | Key Difference from ViTVS |
|---|---|---|---|
| **YuanGongND/ast** — Audio Spectrogram Transformer | ViT encoder for *classification* (not denoising); pretrained on ImageNet; overlapping 16×16 patches | ~2k | Classification only; no decoder, no mask prediction |
| **Sara-Ahmed/ASiT** | ViT self-supervised pretraining on spectrograms; local-global contrastive learning | 29 | Pretraining/classification; no denoising decoder |
| **WangHelin1997/MaskSpec** | MAE-style ViT: random spectrogram patch masking + reconstruction for self-supervised audio pretraining | 50 | Pretraining; masks are *for self-supervision*, not for audio-noise separation |
| **atik666/denoMae** | ViT MAE adapted for RF modulation signal denoising/classification | 8 | RF signals (not audio); classification-focused |
| **ristea/septr** *(SepTr, Interspeech 2022)* | Separable Transformer: two sequential attention blocks, one per time axis and one per frequency axis | – | Audio classification; avoids naïve ViT on spectrograms by separating time/freq attention |
| **Jiawei-Yang/Denoising-ViT** *(DVT, ECCV 2024 Oral)* | Denoises ViT *feature maps* (internal representation artifacts), not audio | 396 | Completely different problem; removes ViT's own internal artifacts |

**Key finding:** No project currently on GitHub does exactly what ViTVS does — a ViT **encoder–decoder** trained to predict a **binary mask** for audio source separation. AST/ASiT use ViT only as an encoder for classification. This is a genuine gap ViTVS fills.

---

### Category 3: State-of-the-Art Audio Denoising / Speech Enhancement

These are the dominant DL-based approaches you're competing against scientifically:

| Project | Architecture | Mask Type | Loss | Performance (VoiceBank-DEMAND) |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| **ruizhecao96/CMGAN** *(INTERSPEECH 2022)* | Conformer + GAN; two-stage magnitude+complex decoder | Soft magnitude + complex ratio mask | MetricGAN (PESQ-optimized adversarial) | PESQ 3.41, SSNR 11.10 dB |
| **seorim0/DCCRN** | Deep Complex Conv-Recurrent; processes complex STFT | Complex IRM (cIRM) | SI-SNR + LMS (perceptual) | Competitive on PESQ/STOI |
| **santi-pdp/segan_pytorch** *(SEGAN+)* | 1D Conv encoder-decoder on raw waveform | No mask; direct waveform mapping | Adversarial (GAN) | ~PESQ 2.98 |
| **JasonSWFu/MetricGAN+** | LSTM-based mask estimator | Soft ratio mask | GAN with PESQ/STOI discriminator | PESQ 3.15 |
| **ZFTurbo/Music-Source-Separation-Training** | Mel-Band RoFormer, BS-RoFormer, Demucs | Complex ratio mask; direct waveform | SI-SNR, L1 | State-of-the-art in music sep |
| **lucidrains/BS-RoFormer** *(ByteDance 2023)* | Band-Split + Rotary Pos. Embeddings + axial attention | Multi-band complex ratio mask | SI-SDR | **SOTA** on MUSDB18 |
| **U-Net variants** (many repos) | CNN encoder-decoder with skip connections | Soft ratio mask (IRM) | MSE or L1 | PESQ ~3.0–3.5 depending on config |

---

## ⚖️ Detailed Technique-by-Technique Comparison

### 1. Audio → Spectrogram Conversion

| Aspect | ViTVS (Your Project) | Typical SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Transform | STFT + ISTFT | STFT, STFT-MDCT, or raw waveform (SEGAN) |
| Frequency bins | 256 (fixed) | 257 (for 512-pt FFT) or mel-scale (128 bins) |
| Spectrogram type | Magnitude (STFT) | Magnitude, or **complex** (real+imag) |
| Phase handling | Noisy phase reused at reconstruction | **Phase-sensitive masks** (PSM) or complex IRM used in SOTA |

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** Reusing the noisy phase during ISTFT is a well-known limitation. SOTA methods (CMGAN, DCCRN) process both magnitude *and* complex STFT to preserve phase coherence. Research ([Kim et al., 2019](https://arxiv.org/abs/1910.10707)) shows this causes a "spectrum mismatch" that BCE/MSE loss can't fully compensate for.

---

### 2. Model Architecture

| Aspect | ViTVS | Typical SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Backbone | Pure ViT encoder + ViT-based decoder | U-Net with skip connections (CMGAN, DCCRN) or Conformer-RNN hybrid |
| Skip connections | ❌ None (pure ViT decoder) | ✅ Essential in U-Net; enables fine-grained detail recovery |
| Receptive field | Global (self-attention over all 256 patches) | U-Net: hierarchical local→global; BS-RoFormer: axial attention per band/time |
| Spectrogram treatment | Treated as a 2D image naïvely | **SepTr** (Interspeech 2022) shows naïve ViT on spectrograms is **suboptimal** — time and frequency axes are semantically different; separate attention per axis works better |
| Parameters | ~87M (depth=12, dim=512, heads=8) | CMGAN: ~1.8M; DCCRN: ~3.7M; BS-RoFormer: ~200M for SOTA |

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** Treating time and frequency axes identically with standard 2D patches is identified as suboptimal in SepTr (Interspeech 2022). The time axis is temporal/causal; the frequency axis represents harmonic structure. BS-RoFormer uses *band-split* processing + *axial attention* (separate attention per axis) specifically to address this.

> ✅ **Strength:** Global attention gives ViTVS the ability to capture long-range temporal correlations in bird calls that CNN/U-Net approaches miss.

---

### 3. Training Target: Ideal Binary Mask (IBM)

| Aspect | ViTVS | Literature |
|---|---|---|
| Mask type | **IBM**: `clean_mag > 0.5 * noisy_mag` → {0, 1} | Research consensus: IBM is a *ceiling/oracle* but **not the best trainable target** |
| IBM threshold | 0.5 × noisy_mag (relative) | Standard IBM uses an absolute SNR threshold (LC, e.g., 0 dB) |
| Soft vs. Hard | Hard binary | IRM (Ideal Ratio Mask) = soft, continuous [0,1] — generally **outperforms IBM** on perceptual quality |
| Phase | Ignores phase | PSM (Phase-Sensitive Mask), cIRM include phase — better SNR |
| IBM pros | Simpler, BCE loss is natural, easier to converge | — |
| IBM cons | Information loss from binarization; mid-frequency TF bins are ambiguously masked | IRM avoids this by producing fractional weights |

From the 2024 PMC review (*"Impact of Mask Type as Training Target"*): IBM is better for **intelligibility**, IRM is better for **quality**. The new QM (Quantized Mask) and PSM+ outperform both. Your IBM's custom threshold `clean_mag > 0.5 * noisy_mag` is actually closer to an **SNR-relative criterion** which is a valid variant, but it's still binary.

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** Hard IBM loses information. The binarization at `0.5 * noisy_mag` is non-standard and may not capture the true signal/noise boundary well, especially for bird calls with harmonic overtones that fall near the threshold.

> ✅ **Strength:** For the bird denoising task specifically (where the goal is *presence/absence* of bird call energy rather than reconstruction fidelity), binary masking may actually be more appropriate than for speech enhancement.

---

### 4. Loss Function

| Aspect | ViTVS | Typical SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Loss | **Binary Cross-Entropy (BCE)** | MSE/L1 (IRM), **SI-SNR** (waveform-domain), MetricGAN (PESQ-optimized), perceptual (LMS, PMSQE) |
| Domain | Mask space | Mix of mask space, spectral space, and waveform domain |
| Phase | Not considered | Consistency loss, phase-sensitive loss in top systems |

> ✅ **Strength:** BCE is the *theoretically correct* loss for a binary classification target (IBM). MSE on a binary target would be equivalent but BCE has better gradient behavior near boundaries.

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** BCE loss optimizes per-pixel mask accuracy, not perceptual audio quality. The field has moved strongly toward **waveform-domain losses** (SI-SNR, PESQ-proxy) because the STFT-to-mask-to-ISTFT pipeline has a fundamental mismatch: minimizing mask BCE doesn't minimize the final audio SDR/PESQ score. CMGAN and MetricGAN+ directly optimize PESQ with a discriminator.

---

### 5. Spectrogram Normalization

| Aspect | ViTVS | Typical SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Normalization | **dB scale** (log magnitude) | Log-mel, dB, or **PCEN** (Per-Channel Energy Normalization) |
| Global vs. local | Presumably global | Per-utterance standardization (mean=0, std=0.5 as in AST) |
| PCEN | Not used | BirdVox uses **PCEN** specifically for bioacoustic monitoring — better handles time-varying noise levels in field recordings |

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** For bird sounds in natural environments, PCEN is demonstrably better than dB normalization. BirdVox research (Lostanlen et al., PLOS ONE 2019) shows PCEN provides automatic gain control per subband, directly addressing the time-varying noise floor in outdoor recordings (wind, rain, distance variation). dB normalization applies a single global transform that doesn't adapt.

> ✅ **Strength:** dB normalization is well-established and keeps the spectrogram values in a range similar to typical image pixel values, which may help the pre-ViT patch embedding learn better.

---

### 6. Input Resolution & Padding Strategy

| Aspect | ViTVS | Typical SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Resolution | Fixed **256×256** with padding/cropping | Variable length; chunked inference with overlap-add |
| Handling variable length | Hard crop/pad | **Overlap-Add (OLA)** synthesis at inference (e.g., Audio ML Noise Reduction uses 32ms windows with 8ms hop + 50% OLA) |
| Patch size | 16×16 → 256 patches | AST: overlapping 16×16 patches with stride 10; BS-RoFormer: 1D per-frame tokens |

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** Hard cropping/padding to 256×256 loses temporal context for long bird recordings and introduces boundary artifacts at crop edges. For a 5-second recording at 22kHz, a 256-frame STFT (~1.5s with hop=256) means you're losing most of the recording or chopping it arbitrarily. OLA or chunked inference with overlap is standard.

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** Fixed 256×256 also means the time resolution is tightly coupled to hop size — changing either requires retraining.

---

### 7. Positional Embeddings

| Aspect | ViTVS | Typical SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Type | **Random init** (learned) | Learned absolute (ViT-base), **Rotary (RoPE)** (BS-RoFormer), 2D sinusoidal (AST) |
| Frequency-time separation | None — treats both axes equally | BS-RoFormer: separate positional encoding per axis |
| Evidence | Baseline for ViT | BS-RoFormer paper shows **rotary embeddings give a "huge improvement" over learned absolute positions** for spectrogram tasks |

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** Random-init learned positional embeddings are the most basic option. For spectrograms specifically, **2D sinusoidal embeddings** better encode the absolute frequency (which has physical meaning — Hz) and temporal position. AST uses pretrained ImageNet patch positions which transfer surprisingly well. Rotary PE (as in BS-RoFormer) enables better length generalization.

---

### 8. Training Framework

| Aspect | ViTVS | Typical Comparable |
|---|---|---|
| Framework | **PyTorch Lightning** | PyTorch (most projects), a few use Lightning |
| Evaluation metrics | Presumably loss curves + visual inspection | PESQ, STOI, SDR, SI-SNR — standardized perceptual + signal metrics |

> ✅ **Strength:** PyTorch Lightning is a genuinely good choice — provides clean training loops, gradient clipping, mixed precision, and checkpoint management with minimal boilerplate. This is an engineering strength.

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** The field expects reported metrics (PESQ, STOI, SDR/SI-SNR). Without these, comparing to published baselines is impossible. BirdSoundsDenoising (WACV 2023) reports pixel-level IoU, SNR improvement, and PESQ-equivalent scores.

---

### 9. Hyperparameters

| Aspect | ViTVS Config | Comparison |
|---|---|---|
| `patch_size=16` | Each patch = 16×16 pixels of spectrogram | AST: 16×16, stride=10 (overlapping); SepTr: separates time/freq patches |
| `depth=12` | ~87M params total | ViT-Base = 12 layers; matches standard ViT-Base scale |
| `dim=512` | Standard ViT-Base dimension | ViT-Base = 768; dim=512 is slightly smaller (ViT-Small scale) |
| `heads=8, mlp_dim=2048` | Standard | ViT-Base: heads=12, mlp=3072; your config is ViT-Small-like |
| `Adam optimizer` | Standard | AdamW (with weight decay) is now the default; CMGAN uses Adam + ReduceLROnPlateau |

> ✅ **Strength:** The config is internally consistent for a ViT-Small-scale model (dim=512, depth=12, heads=8). This is reasonable for a research prototype.

> ⚠️ **Weakness:** Plain `Adam` without weight decay on a 87M-parameter ViT is risky — ViTs are known to overfit without regularization (weight decay, SpecAugment, dropout). Most ViT papers use `AdamW` with `weight_decay=0.05`. The lack of weight decay likely limits generalization.

---

## 📊 Summary Scorecard

| Technique | ViTVS | Industry Norm | Gap Severity |
|---|---|---|---|
| STFT-based spectrogram | ✅ Standard | ✅ | None |
| ViT encoder-decoder | ✅ Novel for audio sep. | ⚠️ Conformer/U-Net dominate | Medium |
| IBM training target | ⚠️ Hard binary, custom threshold | IRM/cIRM/PSM+ preferred | Medium |
| BCE loss | ✅ Correct for IBM | SI-SNR/PESQ losses preferred for audio quality | Medium |
| Noisy phase reuse | ⚠️ Spectrum mismatch | Complex mask or time-domain preferred | High |
| dB normalization | ⚠️ Global only | PCEN better for bioacoustic | Medium |
| Fixed 256×256 | ⚠️ Loses context, boundary artifacts | OLA/chunked inference preferred | High |
| Random positional embed | ⚠️ Baseline only | RoPE/2D-sinusoidal better for spectrograms | Medium |
| Plain Adam | ⚠️ No regularization | AdamW + weight decay standard for ViT | Medium |
| PyTorch Lightning | ✅ Excellent choice | ✅ | None |
| Skip connections | ❌ Absent | U-Net skip connections are critical | High |
| Evaluation metrics | ⚠️ Unclear | PESQ, STOI, SI-SNR required | High |
| Separable time/freq attention | ❌ Naïve 2D | SepTr / BS-RoFormer use axial attention | High |

---

## 🎯 Top Recommendations to Bring ViTVS Closer to SOTA

Here's a prioritized list from highest to lowest impact:

### 🔴 High Impact
1. **Add skip connections** — Wrap the ViT in a U-Net-like structure (UViT / SegFormer style). The decoder should receive encoder features via skip connections at multiple scales. This alone can yield significant PESQ/SDR improvements.

2. **Switch to IRM (Ideal Ratio Mask) + MSE loss** — Replace IBM with `IRM = clean_mag² / (clean_mag² + noise_mag²)` and use MSE. This is a direct upgrade with no architecture change needed.

3. **Use chunked inference with overlap-add** — Rather than padding/cropping to 256×256, chunk the spectrogram into overlapping windows and blend the outputs. This eliminates boundary artifacts on long recordings.

4. **Add standard evaluation metrics** — Report SI-SNR, PESQ, and STOI. Without these, you cannot compare to BirdSoundsDenoising (WACV 2023) or CMGAN.

### 🟡 Medium Impact
5. **Replace plain Adam with AdamW** — Add `weight_decay=0.01–0.05`. ViTs regularize poorly without it.

6. **Try PCEN normalization** — Replace dB scaling with PCEN for better handling of field-recording noise floors (wind, distance variation).

7. **Separable/axial attention** — Consider SepTr-style separate time vs. frequency attention heads, which Interspeech 2022 shows is more suited to spectrograms than naïve 2D ViT.

### 🟢 Lower Priority (Research Directions)
8. **Rotary positional embeddings (RoPE)** — BS-RoFormer shows these outperform learned absolute positions significantly for spectrogram tasks and generalize better to variable-length audio.

9. **Complex spectrogram processing** — Even partially incorporating phase (via Phase-Sensitive Mask or cIRM) would resolve the "spectrum mismatch" issue and improve perceptual quality.

10. **Perceptual loss function** — Add an SI-SNR or differentiable PESQ term alongside BCE to optimize for what you actually care about (audio quality), not just mask accuracy.

---

## 🌟 Genuine Strengths of ViTVS

Despite the gaps, several things about this project are genuinely noteworthy:

1. **Framing bird denoising as image segmentation with a ViT** is novel — no published GitHub project does precisely this combination.
2. **Automated IBM generation** from clean/noisy pairs is far better than the human-labeled masks in BirdSoundsDenoising (WACV 2023), making it scalable.
3. **Global attention** can capture long-range correlations in bird call structure (e.g., harmonic overtones spread across frequency bins) that U-Net's local convolutions miss.
4. **PyTorch Lightning** is a solid engineering choice for reproducibility and scalability.
5. The **bird sound domain** is underserved — most SE research uses VoiceBank-DEMAND (human speech). A ViT-based system tailored to bioacoustic monitoring fills a real gap.

Oke, sudah baca semua codenya dan sudah dapet research perbandingannya. Berikut analisis lengkapnya:

---

# 🔍 Review ViTVS Bird Denoising — Perbandingan dengan Proyek Serupa di GitHub

## 📌 Gambaran Umum

Proyek kamu adalah implementasi **ViT Encoder-Decoder** untuk audio denoising burung, yang mem-framing masalah sebagai **image segmentation** pada spectrogram. Ini genuinely unik — tidak ada proyek GitHub yang melakukan kombinasi ini secara persis sama. Tapi beberapa keputusan teknis ada yang perlu diperhatikan.

---

## ⚖️ Perbandingan Per Teknik

### 1. 🎵 Konversi Audio → Spectrogram (STFT/ISTFT)

| Aspek | Proyek Kamu | Standar di GitHub |
|---|---|---|
| Transform | STFT + ISTFT | ✅ Sama |
| Phase handling | Reuse phase noisy | ❌ SOTA: complex mask (CMGAN, DCCRN) |
| Normalisasi | dB scale (log) | ⚠️ SOTA bioacoustic pakai **PCEN** |

**Masalahnya:** Reusing noisy phase saat ISTFT menyebabkan *spectrum mismatch* — ini diketahui sebagai limitasi besar di paper audio enhancement. Proyek seperti [CMGAN](https://github.com/ruizhecao96/CMGAN) dan [DCCRN](https://github.com/seorim0/DCCRN) memproses **complex spectrogram** (real+imag) sekaligus.

Untuk **bird sounds khususnya**, BirdVox (PLOS ONE 2019) membuktikan **PCEN (Per-Channel Energy Normalization)** jauh lebih baik dari dB normalization karena adapt dengan noise floor yang berubah-ubah (angin, hujan, dll).

---

### 2. 🧠 Arsitektur Model

| Aspek | Proyek Kamu | Proyek Serupa |
|---|---|---|
| Backbone | ViT Encoder + ViT Decoder | CMGAN: Conformer+GAN; DCCRN: Conv-RNN; UNet: CNN |
| Skip connections | ❌ Tidak ada | ✅ **U-Net skip connections** dianggap krusial |
| Receptive field | Global (semua 256 patch sekaligus) | U-Net: lokal→global hierarkis |
| Time/Freq treatment | Disamain (naïve 2D) | BS-RoFormer: axial attention per axis |

**Yang keren:** Global attention ViT bisa nangkep pola long-range di bird call (harmonik yang tersebar di frekuensi) yang CNN tidak bisa.

**Yang lemah:** Paper [SepTr (Interspeech 2022)](https://github.com/ristea/septr) membuktikan kalau treat time dan frequency axis sama-sama di ViT itu **suboptimal** — karena keduanya semantically berbeda. BS-RoFormer (ByteDance, SOTA 2023) pakai *axial attention* terpisah per axis dan *band-split* processing.

---

### 3. 🎭 Training Target: Ideal Binary Mask (IBM)

```bird-denoising-new/src/dataset.py#L52-52
mask = (clean_mag > 0.5 * noisy_mag).astype(np.float32)
```

| Aspek | Proyek Kamu | Literatur |
|---|---|---|
| Mask type | IBM hard binary {0,1} | IRM (soft, continuous) lebih umum |
| Threshold | `0.5 × noisy_mag` (relative) | Standard IBM: threshold SNR absolut (0 dB) |
| Loss | BCE | BCE benar untuk binary, tapi field sudah ke SI-SNR/PESQ |

**Yang oke:** Untuk *bird denoising* spesifik (deteksi ada/tidaknya energi bird call), binary masking mungkin justru lebih cocok daripada soft mask. WACV 2023 ([BirdSoundsDenoising](https://github.com/YoushanZhang/BirdSoundsDenoising)) — proyek yang paling mirip — juga pakai binary mask, tapi **manual-labeled** oleh manusia. Versi kamu yang otomatis via IBM lebih scalable.

**Yang lemah:** Threshold `0.5 * noisy_mag` non-standar dan bisa "salah potong" terutama di harmonic overtones bird call yang magnitude-nya dekat threshold.

---

### 4. 📉 Loss Function

| Aspek | Proyek Kamu | SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Loss | BCE | SI-SNR, MetricGAN (PESQ-optimized), perceptual loss |
| Domain | Mask space | Waveform domain preferred |

BCE adalah pilihan **teoritis benar** untuk binary target. Tapi the field sudah bergerak ke waveform-domain losses karena ada *mismatch fundamental*: minimasi BCE pada mask tidak otomatis minimasi kualitas audio final (PESQ/SDR). CMGAN dan MetricGAN+ langsung optimize PESQ dengan GAN discriminator.

---

### 5. 📐 Fixed 256×256 + Padding/Cropping Strategy

```bird-denoising-new/src/dataset.py#L26-39
def _pad_or_crop_spectrogram(self, spec):
    ...
    spec = spec[:target_size, :]
    ...
    spec = spec[:, :target_size]
```

| Aspek | Proyek Kamu | Standar |
|---|---|---|
| Handling variable length | Hard crop/pad | **Overlap-Add (OLA)** synthesis |
| Context loss | Bisa kehilangan banyak konteks | OLA preserve semua data |
| Boundary artifact | Ada di crop edges | OLA blend dengan overlap |

**Ini salah satu kelemahan terbesar.** Untuk rekaman burung 5 detik di 16kHz dengan hop=256, satu window 256-frame hanya cover ~1.5 detik. Sisa rekaman di-crop atau di-pad dengan nol. Proyek `test.py` sudah ada chunked inference, tapi tanpa overlap → ada boundary artifact antar chunk.

---

### 6. 🔢 Positional Embedding & Hyperparameter

```bird-denoising-new/src/model.py#L60-61
self.pos_embedding = nn.Parameter(torch.randn(1, num_patches, dim))
```

| Aspek | Proyek Kamu | SOTA |
|---|---|---|
| Pos. embedding | Random init (learned) | BS-RoFormer: **RoPE** (rotary) |
| Optimizer | Adam biasa | **AdamW** + weight decay standard untuk ViT |
| Regularization | Dropout saja | AdamW wd=0.05, SpecAugment |

Plain `Adam` tanpa weight decay di model 87M parameter cukup berisiko overfitting. ViT secara umum perlu `AdamW` dengan `weight_decay=0.01–0.05`.

---

### 7. 🛠️ Engineering & Framework

| Aspek | Proyek Kamu | Perbandingan |
|---|---|---|
| Framework | PyTorch Lightning | ✅ Pilihan sangat bagus |
| Resume training | ✅ Otomatis dari latest ckpt | ✅ |
| CLI args | ✅ Argparse | ✅ |
| Evaluation metrics | ❌ Hanya loss | ❌ Tidak ada PESQ, STOI, SI-SNR |

**Kode structure-nya bersih dan well-organized.** Pemisahan `config.py`, `dataset.py`, `model.py`, `lightning_module.py` bagus dan mengikuti best practices. Proyek lain di GitHub banyak yang masih satu file monolith.

---

## 📊 Scorecard Keseluruhan

| Teknik | ViTVS | Skor |
|---|---|---|
| STFT + ISTFT pipeline | Standard ✅ | 8/10 |
| ViT Encoder-Decoder | Novel untuk audio separation ✅ | 8/10 |
| Ideal Binary Mask (IBM) | Non-standard threshold ⚠️ | 5/10 |
| BCE Loss | Benar untuk IBM ✅ | 6/10 |
| Noisy phase reuse | Spectrum mismatch problem ❌ | 4/10 |
| dB normalization | OK tapi PCEN lebih baik untuk bioacoustic ⚠️ | 5/10 |
| Fixed 256×256 crop/pad | Kehilangan konteks, boundary artifact ⚠️ | 4/10 |
| Random pos. embedding | Baseline only ⚠️ | 5/10 |
| Plain Adam | Berisiko overfit untuk ViT ⚠️ | 5/10 |
| Skip connections | Tidak ada ❌ | 3/10 |
| PyTorch Lightning | Pilihan sangat solid ✅ | 9/10 |
| Code organization | Bersih, modular ✅ | 8/10 |
| Evaluation metrics | Tidak ada PESQ/STOI/SI-SNR ❌ | 2/10 |
| **Overall** | | **~5.5/10** |

---

## 🌟 Genuine Strengths

1. **Framing yang unik** — Tidak ada proyek GitHub yang persis melakukan ViT encoder-decoder untuk bird audio denoising. Ini novelty yang nyata.
2. **IBM otomatis** — BirdSoundsDenoising (WACV 2023, closest published peer) butuh *human-annotated mask*. Kamu otomatis via IBM → jauh lebih scalable.
3. **Global attention** — Bisa capture long-range harmonik bird call yang CNN/U-Net miss.
4. **Code quality** — Struktur modular, clean, PyTorch Lightning, CLI, auto-resume training. Engineering-nya di atas rata-rata proyek akademik di GitHub.

---

## 🔴 Top 4 Hal yang Paling Perlu Diperbaiki

1. **Tambahkan Skip Connections** → Wrap dalam UViT/SegFormer-style U-Net structure, bisa langsung naikkan kualitas denoising secara signifikan.
2. **Ganti IBM → IRM** → `IRM = clean_mag² / (clean_mag² + noise_mag²)` + MSE loss. Zero architecture change, langsung lebih bagus.
3. **Tambahkan evaluation metrics** → PESQ, STOI, SI-SNR di `test.py`. Tanpa ini kamu tidak bisa compare ke paper manapun.
4. **Overlap-Add inference** → Ganti hard crop dengan chunked inference + OLA di `test.py` untuk eliminate boundary artifacts.

Mau diimplementasikan yang mana dulu?

## User

coba lihat https://arxiv.org/pdf/2406.09167 dia pakai apa tetap sesuaikan ini dan buat kira kira apa yang bikin bagus project ini, buatkan plannya dulu aja

**Tool Call: Fetch `https://arxiv.org/pdf/2406.09167`**

# Vision Transformer Segmentation for Visual Bird Sound Denoising

###### Abstract

Audio denoising, especially in the context of bird sounds, remains a challenging task due to persistent residual noise. Traditional and deep learning methods often struggle with artificial or low-frequency noise. In this work, we propose ViTVS, a novel approach that leverages the power of the vision transformer (ViT) architecture. ViTVS adeptly combines segmentation techniques to disentangle clean audio from complex signal mixtures. Our key contributions encompass the development of ViTVS, introducing comprehensive, long-range, and multi-scale representations. These contributions directly tackle the limitations inherent in conventional approaches. Extensive experiments demonstrate that ViTVS outperforms state-of-the-art methods, positioning it as a benchmark solution for real-world bird sound denoising applications. Source code is available at: https://github.com/aiai-4/ViVTS.

###### keywords: 

Audio Denoising, Transformer, Segmentation

## 1 Introduction

Audio denoising remains a persistent challenge in modern applications such as teleconferences, social media speech-to-text, and hearing aids  [1]. In the context of bird sound processing, the intricate and varied nature of avian vocalizations presents unique challenges. When addressing these challenges, traditional and deep learning methods are always constrained by issues like artificial noise and low-frequency noise. This has fueled the exploration of innovative solutions tailored for effective bird sound denoising  [2].

Audio denoising methods encompass a spectrum of representations including, time-domain, frequency-domain, and time-frequency domain approaches. Traditional methods, such as the Gaussian mixture model  [3], rely on statistical estimation to extract clean audio from noisy signals. Time-domain algorithms utilize techniques such as Short-Time Fourier Transform (STFT)  [4] and Inverse Short-Time Fourier Transform (ISTFT)  [5]. Additionally, denoising performance is enhanced by applying Wiener filters and LSA estimators  [6, 7]. Deep learning models, such as full convolutional neural networks (FCN), IBM-based DNNs, and Noise2Noise methods, have demonstrated superiority in audio denoising  [8]. These models exhibit effective noise pattern capture and improved learning capabilities, especially with limited training samples  [9, 10, 11, 12, 13]. The vision transformer (ViT)  [14], such as CleanUNet, swin transformer, and CrossVit  [15, 16], has found success in various domains, including audio adaptation tasks. The audio spectrogram transformer showed the potential of attention-based models in audio classification  [17]. Gul and Khan  [8] explored various audio enhancement algorithms, utilizing image U-Net for quality improvement across multiple domains.

In recent years, deep learning applications in bird sound denoising have been extensively explored. Li et al.,  [18] introduced the Deeplabv3+ vision transformer, emphasizing perceptual quality enhancement for noisy audio signals. Zhang and Li  [19] proposed a complex image generation SwinTransformer network, addressing challenges in high-performance audio denoising while emphasizing the quality of generated time-frequency representations. Additionally, Zhang et al.,  [20] explored the influence of recording devices and environmental noise on acoustic index scores, providing implications for bird sound-based assessments. These studies collectively contribute to advancing bird sound denoising through innovative deep-learning approaches  [21, 22, 23, 24, 25]. We assessed our model using ground truth provided by  [20]. The dataset was sourced from natural environments, introducing a potential bias if noise bandwidths perfectly match bird sounds. Most noises have distinct shapes from bird sounds and are removed by our model.

We present a vision transformer for visual (ViTVS) bird sound denoising model, as shown in Fig.  1. By transforming audio denoising into an image segmentation problem, ViTVS harnesses the capabilities of the vision transformer (ViT) architecture. The model includes essential modules: Short-Time Fourier Transform (STFT) for audio-to-image conversion, a vision transformer-based ViTVS model for segmentation, and Inverse Short-Time Fourier Transform (ISTFT) for audio reconstruction.Figure 1: The overview of our ViTVS architecture. The encoder comprises a sequence of self-attention encoder blocks, each executing normalization, patch creation, and embedding layers. The decoder mirrors the encoder with additional operations, including unfolding and output projection, culminating in the final segmentation map. Both encoder and decoder consist of 12 blocks.

ViTVS generates comprehensive, long-range, and multi-scale representations, distinguishing itself from conventional methods. The transformer-based encoder-decoder architecture, exemplified by PtDeepLab  [18], effectively captures and fuses multi-scale features, showcasing its prowess in audio image segmentation. Our contributions are three-fold:
- 1.

We introduce a vision transformer (ViTVS) model for bird sound denoising. Unlike existing ViT models, ViTVS redefines audio denoising as an image segmentation challenge, showcasing its distinctive ability to handle intricate bird sound patterns. The encoder-decoder architecture of ViTVS effectively captures and fuses multi-scale features, surpassing the capabilities of traditional ViT methods.
- 2.

ViTVS encompasses important components by adding s PatchEmbedding layer to transform input audio into image-like patches and developing a SelfAttentionEncoderBlock for multi-head attention.
- 3.

ViTVS achieves state-of-the-art bird sound denoising performance and intricate pattern learning. Leveraging negative log-likelihood loss enhances denoising capabilities, establishing ViTVS as a benchmark.

## 2 Methods

### 2.1 Problem

A noisy audio signal y⁢(t)𝑦𝑡y(t)italic_y ( italic_t ) is modeled as the sum of a clean audio signal x⁢(t)𝑥𝑡x(t)italic_x ( italic_t ) and additive noise ε⁢(t)𝜀𝑡\varepsilon(t)italic_ε ( italic_t )  [26]:
|  | y⁢(t)=x⁢(t)+ε⁢(t)𝑦𝑡𝑥𝑡𝜀𝑡y(t)=x(t)+\varepsilon(t)italic_y ( italic_t ) = italic_x ( italic_t ) + italic_ε ( italic_t ) |  | (1) |

The objective of audio denoising is to learn a mapping ℱℱ\mathcal{F}caligraphic_F that extracts the clean audio component X𝑋Xitalic_X from the mixture audio signal Y={yi}i=1N𝑌superscriptsubscriptsubscript𝑦𝑖𝑖1𝑁Y=\{y_{i}\}_{i=1}^{N}italic_Y = { italic_y start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT } start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i = 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_N end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT, minimizing the approximation error between the estimated denoised audio ℱ⁢(Y)ℱ𝑌\mathcal{F}(Y)caligraphic_F ( italic_Y ) and the clean audio X𝑋Xitalic_X. Our approach also transforms audio denoising into an image segmentation task, aiming to minimize the error between predictions of audio images ℐ={Ii}i=1Nℐsuperscriptsubscriptsubscript𝐼𝑖𝑖1𝑁\mathcal{I}=\{I_{i}\}_{i=1}^{N}caligraphic_I = { italic_I start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT } start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i = 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_N end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT from our model and their corresponding ground truth labeled masks U={ui}i=1N𝑈superscriptsubscriptsubscript𝑢𝑖𝑖1𝑁U=\{u_{i}\}_{i=1}^{N}italic_U = { italic_u start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT } start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i = 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_N end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT.

### 2.2 Motivation

Our motivation stems from the limitations of previous bird sound denoising methods  [4], which struggle to effectively separate bird calls from background noise. Traditional filtering techniques and general-purpose deep learning models are not designed specifically for bird sound tasks. To address these challenges, we propose the ViTVS model, tailored to capture the unique characteristics of avian vocalizations. By transforming audio denoising into an image segmentation task using a novel vision transformer model, we aim to improve denoising performance and accuracy. Our research seeks to advance techniques for analyzing and processing bird vocalizations.

### 2.3 Preliminary

Our model utilizes Short-Time Fourier Transform (STFT) and Inverse Short-Time Fourier Transform (ISTFT) for analyzing and reconstructing audio signals  [6]. We use the absolute value of STFT to segment and identify noise masks, while preserving the original phase in ISTFT for accurate time-domain signal reconstruction. This technique ensures effective noise removal by processing the audio into frames of short-term spectra.

Audio Image Construction: STFT is suitable for non-stationary audio signals since it is capable of dividing the signal into frames and analyzing their short-term spectra:
|  | I=|STFTy⁢(t,f)|.𝐼subscriptSTFT𝑦𝑡𝑓I=\left|\text{STFT}_{y}(t,f)\right|.italic_I = | STFT start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_y end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ( italic_t , italic_f ) | . |  | (2) |

where (I)𝐼(I)( italic_I ) represents the construction of an audio image at time t𝑡titalic_t and frequency f𝑓fitalic_f. We generate audio images using STFT that can convert bird sound audio to image representations.

Denoised Audio Reconstruction: After noise removal in the frequency domain, denoised audio is reconstructed using ISTFT. Filtering noise areas in the frequency domain is guided by predicted masks (u∼=F⁢(I)similar-to𝑢𝐹𝐼\overset{\sim}{u}=F(I)over∼ start_ARG italic_u end_ARG = italic_F ( italic_I ))  [4]:
|  | 𝒪′=𝒪,and𝒪′⁢[u∼<1]=0,formulae-sequencesuperscript𝒪′𝒪andsuperscript𝒪′delimited-[]similar-to𝑢10\mathcal{O^{\prime}}=\mathcal{O},\quad\text{and}\quad\mathcal{O^{\prime}}[% \overset{\sim}{u}<1]=0,caligraphic_O start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ′ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT = caligraphic_O , and caligraphic_O start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ′ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT [ over∼ start_ARG italic_u end_ARG < 1 ] = 0 , |  | (3) |

where 𝒪𝒪\mathcal{O}caligraphic_O is the original audio image, 𝒪′superscript𝒪′\mathcal{O^{\prime}}caligraphic_O start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ′ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT wil get the predicted denoised masks, Eq. ( 4) reconstructs denoised audio (y^⁢(t)^𝑦𝑡\hat{y}(t)over^ start_ARG italic_y end_ARG ( italic_t )) using ISTFT after frequency domain noise removal.
|  | y^⁢(t)=ISTFT⁢(𝒪′)^𝑦𝑡ISTFTsuperscript𝒪′\hat{y}(t)=\text{ISTFT}(\mathcal{O}^{\prime})over^ start_ARG italic_y end_ARG ( italic_t ) = ISTFT ( caligraphic_O start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ′ end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT ) |  | (4) |

## 3 Model Architecture

### 3.1 Input Transformation

Firstly, the model undergoes a meticulous input transformation involving batch normalization and image-to-patch conversion. The input image I𝐼Iitalic_I experiences normalization through Batch Normalization (BN), as depicted in Eq. ( 5):
|  | BN⁢(X)=X−μσ2+ϵ⋅γ+β,BN𝑋⋅𝑋𝜇superscript𝜎2italic-ϵ𝛾𝛽\text{BN}(X)=\frac{X-\mu}{\sqrt{\sigma^{2}+\epsilon}}\cdot\gamma+\beta,BN ( italic_X ) = divide start_ARG italic_X - italic_μ end_ARG start_ARG square-root start_ARG italic_σ start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT + italic_ϵ end_ARG end_ARG ⋅ italic_γ + italic_β , |  | (5) |

where X𝑋Xitalic_X is the input, μ𝜇\muitalic_μ and σ𝜎\sigmaitalic_σ are mean and standard deviation, ϵitalic-ϵ\epsilonitalic_ϵ is a stability constant, γ𝛾\gammaitalic_γ is the scale parameter, and β𝛽\betaitalic_β is the shift parameter. Subsequently, I𝐼Iitalic_I undergoes linear embedding, resulting in a curated sequence X∈ℝN×D𝑋superscriptℝ𝑁𝐷X\in\mathbb{R}^{N\times D}italic_X ∈ blackboard_R start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_N × italic_D end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT, as expressed in Eq. ( 6):
|  | X=Linear⁢(ITP⁢(BN⁢(I))),𝑋LinearITPBN𝐼X=\text{Linear}(\text{ITP}(\text{BN}(I))),italic_X = Linear ( ITP ( BN ( italic_I ) ) ) , |  | (6) |

where ITP denotes ImageToPatches operation.

Image-to-Patch Conversion: The essential image-to-patch function transforms I𝐼Iitalic_I into non-overlapping patches of size p×p𝑝𝑝p\times pitalic_p × italic_p, as defined in Eq. ( 7):
|  | ITP⁢(I)m⁢n=flatten⁢(I(p⁢m):(p⁢m+p−1),(p⁢n):(p⁢n+p−1),:),ITPsubscript𝐼𝑚𝑛flattensubscript𝐼:𝑝𝑚𝑝𝑚𝑝1𝑝𝑛:𝑝𝑛𝑝1:\textbf{ITP}(I)_{mn}=\textbf{flatten}(I_{(pm):(pm+p-1),(pn):(pn+p-1),:}),ITP ( italic_I ) start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_m italic_n end_POSTSUBSCRIPT = flatten ( italic_I start_POSTSUBSCRIPT ( italic_p italic_m ) : ( italic_p italic_m + italic_p - 1 ) , ( italic_p italic_n ) : ( italic_p italic_n + italic_p - 1 ) , : end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ) , |  | (7) |

where I(p⁢m):(p⁢m+p−1),(p⁢n):(p⁢n+p−1),:subscript𝐼:𝑝𝑚𝑝𝑚𝑝1𝑝𝑛:𝑝𝑛𝑝1:I_{(pm):(pm+p-1),(pn):(pn+p-1),:}italic_I start_POSTSUBSCRIPT ( italic_p italic_m ) : ( italic_p italic_m + italic_p - 1 ) , ( italic_p italic_n ) : ( italic_p italic_n + italic_p - 1 ) , : end_POSTSUBSCRIPT selects the patch at position (m,n)𝑚𝑛(m,n)( italic_m , italic_n ) in the image, and flatten reshapes this patch into a flattened vector. We ensure proper handling of patch edges during the reassembly of these patches into a complete image.

### 3.2 Encoder

In ViTVS model, the encoder and decoder play crucial roles in their architectures. The encoder serves as the backbone, consisting of self-attention-based blocks meticulously organized into 12 layers. Self-Attention Encoder Block: Each encoder block (i𝑖iitalic_i) includes self-attention mechanisms and feedforward neural networks  [27], complemented by layer normalization. The progression within an encoder block is expressed in Eqs.( 8), ( 9), and ( 10):
|  | Attention_OutputisubscriptAttention_Output𝑖\displaystyle\text{Attention\_Output}_{i}Attention_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT | =MultiheadAttention⁢(LN⁢(Xi)),absentMultiheadAttentionLNsubscript𝑋𝑖\displaystyle=\text{MultiheadAttention}(\text{LN}(X_{i})),= MultiheadAttention ( LN ( italic_X start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ) ) , |  | (8) |
|  | MLP_OutputisubscriptMLP_Output𝑖\displaystyle\text{MLP\_Output}_{i}MLP_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT | =MLP⁢(LN⁢(Attention_Outputi)),absentMLPLNsubscriptAttention_Output𝑖\displaystyle=\text{MLP}(\text{LN}(\text{Attention\_Output}_{i})),= MLP ( LN ( Attention_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ) ) , |  | (9) |
|  | Xi+1subscript𝑋𝑖1\displaystyle X_{i+1}italic_X start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i + 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT | =Xi+MLP_Outputi,absentsubscript𝑋𝑖subscriptMLP_Output𝑖\displaystyle=X_{i}+\text{MLP\_Output}_{i},= italic_X start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT + MLP_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , |  | (10) |

Multihead Self-Attention: The intricate operation of queries Q𝑄Qitalic_Q, keys K𝐾Kitalic_K, and values V𝑉Vitalic_V unfolds through linear projections of X𝑋Xitalic_X. The nuances of this process are encapsulated in Eqs. ( 11) and ( 12):
|  | Q𝑄\displaystyle Qitalic_Q | =X⋅WQ,absent⋅𝑋subscript𝑊𝑄\displaystyle=X\cdot W_{Q},= italic_X ⋅ italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_Q end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , | K𝐾\displaystyle\quad Kitalic_K | =X⋅WK,absent⋅𝑋subscript𝑊𝐾\displaystyle=X\cdot W_{K},= italic_X ⋅ italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_K end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , | V𝑉\displaystyle\quad Vitalic_V | =X⋅WV,absent⋅𝑋subscript𝑊𝑉\displaystyle=X\cdot W_{V},= italic_X ⋅ italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_V end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , |  | (11) |
|  | Attention_Scores=softmax⁢(Q⁢KTDk)⋅V,Attention_Scores⋅softmax𝑄superscript𝐾𝑇subscript𝐷𝑘𝑉\text{Attention\_Scores}=\text{softmax}\left(\frac{QK^{T}}{\sqrt{D_{k}}}\right% )\cdot V,Attention_Scores = softmax ( divide start_ARG italic_Q italic_K start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_T end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT end_ARG start_ARG square-root start_ARG italic_D start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_k end_POSTSUBSCRIPT end_ARG end_ARG ) ⋅ italic_V , |  | (12) |

where X𝑋Xitalic_X is the input sequence at a certain layer, WQsubscript𝑊𝑄W_{Q}italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_Q end_POSTSUBSCRIPT, WKsubscript𝑊𝐾W_{K}italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_K end_POSTSUBSCRIPT, and WVsubscript𝑊𝑉W_{V}italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_V end_POSTSUBSCRIPT are learnable weight matrices and Dksubscript𝐷𝑘D_{k}italic_D start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_k end_POSTSUBSCRIPT is the dimension of queries and keys  [27].

Feedforward Neural Network (MLP): The Multi-Layer Perceptron (MLP) works with two linear layers and GELU activation, as portrayed in Eq. ( 13):
|  | MLP⁢(X)=GELU⁢(X⋅W1+b1)⋅W2+b2,MLP𝑋⋅GELU⋅𝑋subscript𝑊1subscript𝑏1subscript𝑊2subscript𝑏2\text{MLP}(X)=\text{GELU}(X\cdot W_{1}+b_{1})\cdot W_{2}+b_{2},MLP ( italic_X ) = GELU ( italic_X ⋅ italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT + italic_b start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ) ⋅ italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT + italic_b start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , |  | (13) |

where W1subscript𝑊1W_{1}italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT, W2subscript𝑊2W_{2}italic_W start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT, b1subscript𝑏1b_{1}italic_b start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT, and b2subscript𝑏2b_{2}italic_b start_POSTSUBSCRIPT 2 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT represent the weights matrix and biases vectors that the model learns through training to make predictions based on the input X𝑋Xitalic_X. The subscripts 1111 and 2222 denote the layers of the MLP.

### 3.3 Decoder

The decoder mirrors the encoder structure but incorporates an output projection layer, also featuring 12 layers.

Decoder Block: Each decoder block entails a self-attention encoder block, layer normalization, and an MLP. The baton passes from one block to the next, as expressed in Eqs. ( 14),  ( 15), and ( 16):
|  | Attention_OutputisubscriptAttention_Output𝑖\displaystyle\text{Attention\_Output}_{i}Attention_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT | =SelfAttentionEncoderBlock⁢(LN⁢(Xi)),absentSelfAttentionEncoderBlockLNsubscript𝑋𝑖\displaystyle=\text{SelfAttentionEncoderBlock}(\text{LN}(X_{i})),= SelfAttentionEncoderBlock ( LN ( italic_X start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ) ) , |  | (14) |
|  | MLP_OutputisubscriptMLP_Output𝑖\displaystyle\text{MLP\_Output}_{i}MLP_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT | =MLP⁢(LN⁢(Attention_Outputi)),absentMLPLNsubscriptAttention_Output𝑖\displaystyle=\text{MLP}(\text{LN}(\text{Attention\_Output}_{i})),= MLP ( LN ( Attention_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ) ) , |  | (15) |
|  | Xi+1subscript𝑋𝑖1\displaystyle X_{i+1}italic_X start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i + 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT | =Xi+MLP_Outputi,absentsubscript𝑋𝑖subscriptMLP_Output𝑖\displaystyle=X_{i}+\text{MLP\_Output}_{i},= italic_X start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT + MLP_Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT , |  | (16) |

Output Projection: The final step involves projecting the output to the original image dimensions through a linear layer, followed by a folding process, as defined in Eq. ( 17):
|  | Output=Fold⁢(Linear⁢(X)).OutputFoldLinear𝑋\text{Output}=\text{Fold}(\text{Linear}(X)).Output = Fold ( Linear ( italic_X ) ) . |  | (17) |

In short, both the encoder and decoder architectures comprise 12 layers, each housing self-attention blocks, layer normalization, and multi-layer perceptrons (MLPs).

### 3.4 Loss Function and Algorithm

Loss Function: We train our ViTVS model using a negative log-likelihood loss (NLL)  [28], expressed in Eq. ( 18):
|  | Loss=−1N⁢∑i=1Nlog⁡(exp⁡(Outputi⁢[Mi])∑j=1Cexp⁡(Outputi⁢[j])),Loss1𝑁superscriptsubscript𝑖1𝑁subscriptOutput𝑖delimited-[]subscript𝑀𝑖superscriptsubscript𝑗1𝐶subscriptOutput𝑖delimited-[]𝑗\text{Loss}=-\frac{1}{N}\sum_{i=1}^{N}\log\left(\frac{\exp(\text{Output}_{i}[M% _{i}])}{\sum_{j=1}^{C}\exp(\text{Output}_{i}[j])}\right),Loss = - divide start_ARG 1 end_ARG start_ARG italic_N end_ARG ∑ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i = 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_N end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT roman_log ( divide start_ARG roman_exp ( Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT [ italic_M start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT ] ) end_ARG start_ARG ∑ start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_j = 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_C end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT roman_exp ( Output start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT [ italic_j ] ) end_ARG ) , |  | (18) |

where N𝑁Nitalic_N denotes the number of pixels, C𝐶Citalic_C signifies the number of classes, j𝑗jitalic_j is a summation index representing each class (1111 to C𝐶Citalic_C). and Misubscript𝑀𝑖M_{i}italic_M start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT represents the ground truth label for pixel i𝑖iitalic_i.

This loss function quantifies dissimilarity between predicted and ground truth labels, fostering the model to generate accurate and contextually relevant segmentation maps. The negative log-likelihood  [28] penalizes incorrect predictions, contributing to a robust learning process. The log-softmax ensures numerical stability during computation.

Training Algorithm.We train our ViTVS model using Alg.  1.Algorithm 1  Vision Transformer Segmentation for Visual Bird Sound Denoising0:  Noisy audio signals Y={yi}i=1N𝑌superscriptsubscriptsubscript𝑦𝑖𝑖1𝑁Y=\{y_{i}\}_{i=1}^{N}italic_Y = { italic_y start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT } start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i = 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_N end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT and labeled mask images M={mi}i=1N𝑀superscriptsubscriptsubscript𝑚𝑖𝑖1𝑁M=\{m_{i}\}_{i=1}^{N}italic_M = { italic_m start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i end_POSTSUBSCRIPT } start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_i = 1 end_POSTSUBSCRIPT start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_N end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT, where N𝑁Nitalic_N is the total number of audio samples.0:  Denoised audio signals ℱ⁢(Y)ℱ𝑌\mathcal{F}(Y)caligraphic_F ( italic_Y )1:  Generate audio images ℐℐ\mathcal{I}caligraphic_I using Eq. (2)2:  Initialize vision transformer model with encoder (12 blocks), decoder (12 blocks), and likelihood loss function.3:  for iter=1iter1\text{iter}=1iter = 1 to I⁢I𝐼𝐼IIitalic_I italic_I do4:     for k=1𝑘1k=1italic_k = 1 to nBsubscript𝑛𝐵n_{B}italic_n start_POSTSUBSCRIPT italic_B end_POSTSUBSCRIPT do5:        Extract batch-wise data: Iksuperscript𝐼𝑘I^{k}italic_I start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_k end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT and Mksuperscript𝑀𝑘M^{k}italic_M start_POSTSUPERSCRIPT italic_k end_POSTSUPERSCRIPT sampled from ℐℐ\mathcal{I}caligraphic_I and M𝑀Mitalic_M using Eqs. (5),  (6) and  (7).6:        Encode audio images using the Vision Transformer encoder with 12 blocks using Eqs. (8),  (9), and  (10).7:        Obtain segmentation using the vision transformer decoder with 12 blocks using Eq. (17).8:        Calculate likelihood loss using the specified likelihood loss function using Eq. (18).9:        Backward pass and update model parameters.10:     end for11:  end for12:  Obtain the clean frequency domain using Eq. (3)13:  Output the denoised audio signals using Eq. (4)

## 4 Experiments

### 4.1 Implementation details

To ensure the efficacy and robustness of our approach, we utilized PyTorch version 2.0.1 in conjunction with torchvision version 0.15.2. This framework was complemented by CUDA version 11.7, leveraging parallel processing capabilities on the NVIDIA GeForce RTX 4070 GPU. The learning rate is set to 5⁢e−55𝑒55e-55 italic_e - 5 with an AdamW optimizer, and the weight decay is adjusted to 5e-4. Further, we resize input images to 256 × 256 × 3 with a mini-batch size of 8 for 100 epochs.Figure 2: Segmentation results comparisons. The leftmost column is the original audio image. The ground truth is the labeled mask. 

### 4.2 Datasets

Our model is evaluated using the BirdSoundsDenoising dataset, which contains 14,120 audio signals lasting one to fifteen seconds each, split into training (10,000), validation (1,400), and testing (2,720) sets  [4]. This dataset stands out by featuring natural environmental noises—like wind, waterfalls, and rain—instead of artificial noise.

### 4.3 Results

We evaluate our ViTVS model against existing methods in terms of learning efficacy, capability, and qualitative outcomes. We use three key metrics—F1, IoU, and Dice—for image segmentation performance assessment  [4], and the signal-to-distortion ratio (SDR) for audio denoising efficacy, as outlined in  [18]. Higher scores in these metrics indicate better segmentation and denoising performance, reflecting closer alignment with ground truth, which calculated based on labeled masks rather than real-world clean bird sounds. As shown in Tab.  1, Fig.  1, and Fig.  2, our model significantly enhances denoising performance, paving the way for applications in bird species classification and audio signal enhancement.

### 4.4 Performance Comparison

Fig.  2 shows the comparisons of five best baseline segmentation models. The performance of various audio denoising methods is detailed in Tab.  1, including F⁢1𝐹1F1italic_F 1 score, Intersection over Union (I⁢o⁢U𝐼𝑜𝑈IoUitalic_I italic_o italic_U), Dice score, and S⁢D⁢R𝑆𝐷𝑅SDRitalic_S italic_D italic_R on both validation and test sets. Among these methods, ViTVS stands out, demonstrating robust denoising capabilities. ViTVS achieves the highest F⁢1𝐹1F1italic_F 1, I⁢o⁢U𝐼𝑜𝑈IoUitalic_I italic_o italic_U and D⁢i⁢c⁢e𝐷𝑖𝑐𝑒Diceitalic_D italic_i italic_c italic_e scores on both validation and test sets, highlighting its superior segmentation accuracy. The S⁢D⁢R𝑆𝐷𝑅SDRitalic_S italic_D italic_R values reinforce ViTVS’s excellence in denoising, positioning it as a compelling choice for audio denoising. ViTVS consistently outperforms state-of-the-art methods across multiple metrics, emphasizing its efficacy and potential for real-world applications.

To investigate architectural variations and determine the optimal configuration, we conducted an ablation study on our Vision Transformer Segmentation (ViTVS) model. The study focused on comparing variants, specifically the number of blocks in both the encoder and decoder. We trained five variants with block configurations ranging from 4 to 20, evaluating their performance on validation and test sets using I⁢o⁢U𝐼𝑜𝑈IoUitalic_I italic_o italic_U, D⁢i⁢c⁢e𝐷𝑖𝑐𝑒Diceitalic_D italic_i italic_c italic_e, and F⁢1𝐹1F1italic_F 1 scores. Notably, increasing blocks from 4 to 12 substantially improved denoising capabilities, emphasizing the pivotal role of block count. Intriguingly, further experimentation with 16 blocks did not yield additional benefits, suggesting 12 blocks strike an optimal balance between complexity and performance. The ViTVS 12-block variant showcased superior results compared to its 4, 5, 9, 16, and 20-block counterparts in terms of IoU, Dice, and F1 scores, underscoring the significance of a finely tuned model for optimal denoising. ## 5 Discussion

Our ViTVS model demonstrates superior performance compared to the CNN-based PtDeepLab model  [18] and eleven other state-of-the-art segmentation and denoising methods. It excels in segmentation results and enhances representation capacity by effectively capturing multi-scale information for detailed context patterning. The ablation study results, shown in Tab.  2, and the segmented mask quality in Fig.  2 validate our model’s robustness in preserving essential clean signals. While converting audio denoising to segmentation proposed in  [4], our unique bird vision-transformed segmentation model marks the first of its kind to notably enhance denoising tasks.

## 6 Conclusion

In this paper, we introduce a vision transformer for a visual bird sound denoising model (ViTVS). Our ViTVS model is designed with a self-attention mechanism, patch-based processing, layer normalization, and multi-layer perceptrons to capture long-range dependencies and effectively handle diverse input sizes. ViTVS exhibits superior performance to state-of-the-art methods, as evidenced by extensive experimental evaluations, including comparisons with CNN-based self-attention and diffusion models. Therefore, our developed ViTVS model is suitable for bird sound denoising.

## Assistant

Sekarang saya sudah baca paper aslinya secara lengkap. Ini adalah paper yang **menjadi referensi langsung** dari project kamu! Ini adalah paper ViTVS yang dipublish di **Interspeech 2024**. Sekarang bisa bikin perbandingan yang jauh lebih akurat dan rencana improvement yang sesuai.
